  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

I look out the window, and I see him. He’s tall, lean a</span>
  <span id="freeText16120945615743510446" style="display:none">My disease is as rare as it is famous. It’s a form of Severe Combined Immunodeficiency, but basically, I’m allergic to the world. I don’t leave my house, have not left my house in fifteen years. The only people I ever see are my mom and my nurse, Carla.<br /><br />But then one day, a moving truck arrives. New next door neighbors. I look out the window, and I see him. He’s tall, lean and wearing all black—black t-shirt, black jeans, black sneakers and a black knit cap that covers his hair completely. He catches me looking and stares at me. I stare right back. His name is Olly. I want to learn everything about him, and I do. I learn that he is funny and fierce. I learn that his eyes are Atlantic Ocean-blue and that his vice is stealing silverware. I learn that when I talk to him, my whole world opens up, and I feel myself starting to change—starting to want things. To want out of my bubble. To want everything, everything the world has to offer.<br /><br />Maybe we can’t predict the future, but we can predict some things. For example, I am certainly going to fall in love with Olly. It’s almost certainly going to be a disaster.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16120945615743510446" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<div id="review_1272791077" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1272791077" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1272791077?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1272791077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6140937845583852055">This is a book I expected to <b>LOVE</b>.<br/>It's a book many of my GR friends have loved.<br/>It's a book I <i>
  <b>was</b>
</i> kind of liking until the thing happens...<br/><br/>...the thing that just cheapens the entire story.<br/><br/>I have been dying to read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18692431.Everything__Everything' title='Everything, Everything by Nicola Yoon' rel='nofollow noopener'>Everything, Everything</a>. The reviews were all positive, it received a Kirkus star, it sounded so <i>different</i>... all these reasons added up to one of my most anticipated reads of the year. <br/><br/>And it started quite beautifully-written with diverse characters, including an Afro-Asian narrator</span>
  <span id="freeText6140937845583852055" style="display:none">This is a book I expected to <b>LOVE</b>.<br />It's a book many of my GR friends have loved.<br />It's a book I <i>
  <b>was</b>
</i> kind of liking until the thing happens...<br /><br />...the thing that just cheapens the entire story.<br /><br />I have been dying to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18692431.Everything__Everything" title="Everything, Everything by Nicola Yoon" rel="nofollow noopener">Everything, Everything</a>. The reviews were all positive, it received a Kirkus star, it sounded so <i>different</i>... all these reasons added up to one of my most anticipated reads of the year. <br /><br />And it started quite beautifully-written with diverse characters, including an Afro-Asian narrator called Madeline. Madeline's condition aside - being allergic to the entire world outside her sterile home - it quickly became evident that the book wasn't as unique as I'd anticipated. It follows in the footsteps of the great doomed love cheesefest of our time - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11870085.The_Fault_in_Our_Stars" title="The Fault in Our Stars by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fault in Our Stars</a> - and other clones like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18460392.All_the_Bright_Places" title="All the Bright Places by Jennifer Niven" rel="nofollow noopener">All the Bright Places</a>.<br /><br />Unlike the aforementioned two, though, I found myself enjoying this book. It was more cheesy than sweet, in my opinion, but I still enjoyed the emphasis on the human need for <b>more</b>. I thought Madeline was incredibly selfish at times, but this offered complexity to her character and her yearning was palpable:<br /><br /><i>“For the first time in a long time, I want more than I have.”<br /><br />“Wanting just leads to more wanting. There’s no end to desire.”</i><br /><br />I did get a whiff of instalove. It's like Madeline first sets her eyes on Olly and her whole concept of the world changes. But I did like the build of their relationship after this, through miming at the window, chatting online and sharing poems, jokes and philosophical musings with one another. Even if Olly is a classic manic pixie dream boy who exists only to make Madeline want more.<br /><br />And then... <b>the thing</b>. The twist that turns a story about an unusual, impossible relationship into JUST ANOTHER YA ROMANCE.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>If you don't care about being spoiled:</u>
</b> <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Madeline discovers that it's all a lie! She isn't actually sick and her mother essentially made it up to protect her and keep her in the house after her dad and brother died (her mother isn't evil, just mentally ill).<br /><br />But it's so cheap because the author has built up this romance around the concept of one person having an illness that doesn't allow them to leave the house (an interesting idea) and then once they're all lurved up, she smashes the concept with a hammer and it crumbles into a story about two relatively normal teens in love. I thought we were doomed but... YAY, now we can be together! It was the laziest way to tag a happy ending onto the novel.<br /><br />Not only this, but how the hell did her mom get away with it for 18 years? Are we seriously supposed to believe that no one questioned it? Her mom is a doctor, but seriously - wtf?! She never had an official diagnosis! Did she never see any other doctors? This is set in California where I'm pretty sure they don't just let parents lock their kids in the house without some seriously good reason. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />It wasn't a great book before, but I was enjoying it. The ending, however, ruined the entire thing.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6140937845583852055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1391903453" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1391903453" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1391903453?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1391903453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4783059049449191463">This book is about a the most special different unique girl half black-half-Japanese girl in the world who has a super ultra extraordinarily rare disease which nobody can figure out which makes her allergic to everything, therefore she has to stay inside all day, who meets a boy who moves in next door, and <b>it is exactly as boring as it sounds</b>. There is such a thing as trying too hard.<br/><br/>I feel nothing for our doomed character. I don't really care that she could kick the bucket at any moment as she </span>
  <span id="freeText4783059049449191463" style="display:none">This book is about a the most special different unique girl half black-half-Japanese girl in the world who has a super ultra extraordinarily rare disease which nobody can figure out which makes her allergic to everything, therefore she has to stay inside all day, who meets a boy who moves in next door, and <b>it is exactly as boring as it sounds</b>. There is such a thing as trying too hard.<br /><br />I feel nothing for our doomed character. I don't really care that she could kick the bucket at any moment as she randomly develops an allergy to her clothes, her mom, the furniture. I don't care about her. I don't feel bad for her. She is sheltered, dull, emotionally underdeveloped. I have no fucks to give about whatever silly ass random hopes and wishes and dreams she has (go to Hawaii! Whoo! That's my dream too. Whoop de doo).<br /><br />There are cute little drawings! Whoo! There are book spoilers (the mouse in <i>Flowers for Algernon</i> died, and that book did make me cry in 5th grade).<br /><br />The Cute Boy Next Door(tm) sends her emails! They slowly fall in love! <br /><br />The end. It is that boring. Who gives a fuck?<br /><br />In all seriousness, I don't really read contemporary books, and I have criterias for them. They're supposed to make me feel for the main character. I want to suffer along with them. I want to fall in love along with them. I want to experience their joy, their pain. In a book in which a character is pretty much doomed from the start, I want to live each breath with them like it was their last.<br /><br />This book did nothing for me. There's a Bundt cake that "commits suicide" in the book. I felt more emotion for that cake than I did for anyone in this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4783059049449191463" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2491708484" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2491708484" />
    <a title="NReads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34369915-nreads"><img alt="NReads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600781665p2/34369915.jpg" /></a>

<div id="review_2136964082" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2136964082" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2136964082?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=ya-series">ya-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=mary-sue-i-will-kill-you">mary-sue-i-will-kill-you</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2136964082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11887744020692532809"><b>Generic Teen Book on Steroids.</b><br/><br/><b>
  <u>Cast of Characters:</u>
</b><br/>--<b>Critically Ill Teen</b> with a heart of gold. Yes, she's suffering but more importantly, <i>will she find love?</i><br/>--<b>Overbearing Mother</b> who keeps unreasonable tight leash on her 18 year old daughter because <i>she loves her baby girl</i><br/>--<b>Edgy Angsty Hottie</b> with a heart of gold AND emotional baggage. He has abs, he likes math and man-oh-man can he bat those baby blues. <i>Swoon</i><br/>--<b>Abusive Father</b> - one-dimensional jerk that beats <b>Edgy, Angsty Hottie's</b> family around</span>
  <span id="freeText11887744020692532809" style="display:none"><b>Generic Teen Book on Steroids.</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Cast of Characters:</u>
</b><br />--<b>Critically Ill Teen</b> with a heart of gold. Yes, she's suffering but more importantly, <i>will she find love?</i><br />--<b>Overbearing Mother</b> who keeps unreasonable tight leash on her 18 year old daughter because <i>she loves her baby girl</i><br />--<b>Edgy Angsty Hottie</b> with a heart of gold AND emotional baggage. He has abs, he likes math and man-oh-man can he bat those baby blues. <i>Swoon</i><br />--<b>Abusive Father</b> - one-dimensional jerk that beats <b>Edgy, Angsty Hottie's</b> family around. Was given a half-hearted backstory (like the other family members)<br />--<b>Gay Music-Loving Friend</b>, totally accepted by friends, hiding it from family (who I am fairly convinced only shows to check this one off the box) (he literally appears to once, drops some sage advice and is never mentioned again)<br /><br /><b>Essentially...</b> <br /><br />Critically Ill Teen has a<b> long-term, incurable immunodeficiency </b>that essentially imprisons her in her own home. <br /><br />Edgy Angsty Hottie moves next door and does all sorts of <b>edgy and angsty and hottie things. </b><br /><br />Crit-Ill-Teen has to decide - will she follow the rules that<b>
  <i> literally </i>
</b>keep her alive? Or will she throw <b>
  <i>everything </i>
</b>away for one PG kiss and over-the-jeans-butt-touch? <br /><br />(I think you already know her answer).<br /><br />To channel my (already) long rant, I will limit myself to: <b> the Boy Tastes, the Smex Scenes, the Idiocy of Teenagers and the Cop-Out Ending.</b><br /><br /><u>
  <b>The Boy Tastes - <i>cause minty-fresh breath is sooo last year</i></b>
</u><br /><br />Seriously, <b>WHY </b> do all these YA teen boys have tastes? <blockquote>
  <i> He tastes like salted caramel and sunshine</i>
</blockquote> Ah yes, he must be one of those guys always chewing on caramels flavored with the sun to get that<b> extra zingy kissing boost</b>.<blockquote><i> He tastes like nothing I've ever experienced. Like hope and possibility and the future </i> </blockquote>...more like, he tastes like <b>
  <i>germs and diseases</i>
</b> because you have a compromised immune system. <br /><br /><b>GURL - why is<i> his tongue in your mouth??</i></b><br /><br /><u>
  <b>The Smex Scenes - <i> cause nothing says YA like complete incompetence...</i></b>
</u><br /><br />Look, I know she's pretty isolated, but <b>she has the internet.</b> She knows how to Google. There are no excuses for moments like this: <blockquote> <i> I kiss my way across the landscape of him. Down to his toes and back up again.</i> </blockquote> <b>Girl. What. Are. You. Doing.</b><br /><br /> And, to top it all off:<blockquote>
  <i>We are wordless and then we are joined</i>
</blockquote> (gracefully fade to black). I am 99% sure it did not go like that. She was probably making another pass at kissing his toes at some point.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>The Idiocy of Teenagers - <i>it's totally not like you lived with this disease your entire life...right?</i></b>
</u><br /><br /><b>Critically Ill Teen</b> complete disregard for personal safety regarding her disease <b> drove me absolutely mad.</b><br /><br />How can you grow up with an<b> incurable, potentially fatal disease</b> and not know/stay within your limits? HOW?<blockquote>
  <i>Everything's a risk. Not doing anything's a risk. It's up to you</i>
</blockquote>It's the equivalent of peanut-allergy-kid nibbling on a reese's PB cup every couple of weeks too see what would happen.<br /><br />Throughout this book, this girl makes one dumb decision after another - it's like...<b>
  <i>do you even know you have a disease?</i>
</b> <br /><br />There's barely anything done to keep her safe. <br /><br />Technically, there's an airlock and a no-touching rule but <b>Edgy, Angsty Hottie</b> still touches so much of the house and the <b>Overbearing Mother</b> (who's a DOCTOR) seems to disregard even the most basic decontamination rules...<br /><br />I know that the illness is supposed to be second to the romance but to use such a serious illness as a YA plot device? The least you can do is make it realistic.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>The Cop-Out Ending - <i>I read this much story...for THIS?</i></b>
</u><br /><br /> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <b>It was all a lie the entire time! </b><br /><br />She was never sick! Thank goodness because now the <b>star-crossed lovers can be together. </b><br /><br />BUT WAIT! There's more. <br /><br />By bubbling this child, she really <i>does</i> have a version of the disease. <br /><br />It feels like the author was always angling for this and <b>never intended to have a real ending</b> for the characters.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br />Narrated by Bahni Turpin and Robbie Daymond - they were pretty good! Enjoyable audio quality at least!<br /><br /><a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11887744020692532809" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1433041926" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1433041926" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1433041926?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30604861-emma-giordano?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1433041926" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14048668796147456998">3 Stars. Unfortunately, I was a little let down by Everything Everything. I have heard people raving about it since 2015, I've been dying to read it since 2015. I can't exactly tell if it was just overhyped (by others and myself) or if the book just all around was not the best for me.<br/><br/>The overarching positive thing I have to say about this book is that it was entertaining. Although I wasn't 100% satisfied with the story as a whole, I wanted to keep reading. It was addicting and amusing, and it wa</span>
  <span id="freeText14048668796147456998" style="display:none">3 Stars. Unfortunately, I was a little let down by Everything Everything. I have heard people raving about it since 2015, I've been dying to read it since 2015. I can't exactly tell if it was just overhyped (by others and myself) or if the book just all around was not the best for me.<br /><br />The overarching positive thing I have to say about this book is that it was entertaining. Although I wasn't 100% satisfied with the story as a whole, I wanted to keep reading. It was addicting and amusing, and it was an enjoyable read. Also, we get a main character who is biracial (African American/Japanese). Biracial characters don't always get their own stories in YA, so I was glad to see some positive representation on this front. <br /><br />I also really liked Olly and Maddie together. I thought they complimented each other well. Olly was always looking out for Maddie's best interests and was respectful and attentive to her needs. These are the types of love interests we need in YA and I was happy to see them together.<br /><br />That being said, I was irked by quite a lot of this book. Firstly, I felt there was way too much of a focus on romance being Maddie's drive to "truly live." I was very happy that at certain points, Maddie wanted to go outside for herself, to not feel restricted, and to be free. I may not agree with some of the risks Maddie took with her perceived condition, but if there was a reason for her to take those risks, a sense of taking control of your life and living for *you* is what I was glad to see. Unfortunately, I felt at a lot of time, that individual desire was overshadowed by a desire for love. There are so many points in this book where Maddie relays to Oly that she <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ "never would have gone outside if it wasn't for him", "wanted Olly to have a girlfriend who could do the same things as him" etc.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I felt that there was too much of a focus on the presence of Olly shaping Maddie's decisions, and at times her personal discovery was overshadowed by her love for him. I left this book, not with the message that you should live your life to the fullest, but that Maddie was okay with sacrificing her personal health for love, and that's something I'm vehemently against. Had there been a focus on Maddie accepting she made risky decisions for Olly and that she had a new-found desire to make those decisions for herself only, I would have been more okay with it. But whatever efforts were made to squash the idea that "putting yourself at risk is romantic" were not strong enough for me to condone those actions.<br /><br />(This section technically constitutes as "spoilers" so I'll hide it, but if you've seen the trailer or know what decisions of Maddie's that I'm talking about, you won't be spoiled.) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I was somewhat appalled at how little Maddie seemed concerned for her health when she was outside and went to Hawaii?? Let me be clear that I do not have SCID, I have no experience with SCID or other medical disabilities, so what I'm saying here is HELLA IREELEVANT and just my personal interpretation. AKA I'm not attempting to speak for people with conditions like SCID. But I was truly in shock that Maddie did not often make enough comments, even to herself, about the impending risk of getting ill and dying? This girl has spent her entire life being told she has a high probability of dying if she goes outside. Yet she is in an entirely new environment, swimming in the ocean, in contact with people she has never met, eating new foods, wearing new textiles. I just could not understand how this girl could not be nervous 24/7 about getting sick when she has spent her life being told everything she is currently doing will potentially make her sick. It honestly took away a huge chunk of the authenticity of the story and felt entirely unrealistic in my opinion, but again, I have no experience with this matter, so maybe my perception is skewed and Maddie had fully reasonable reactions to her new experiences.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Now we get to the issues with representation and research regarding SCID, which I'm not qualified to talk about, but feel it's important to address regardless.<br />*I am incapable of accurately describing the issues of representation in Everything Everything.<br />I read a review from Disability in Kidlit which wonderfully expressing why this book is harmful to people with disabilities. It spoils the ending for those of you that have not read it, but I feel it's an extremely well written review and I'd really recommend checking it out: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://disabilityinkidlit.com/2015/09/04/review-everything-everything-by-nicola-yoon/">http://disabilityinkidlit.com/2015/09...</a> <br />I've heard in passing that Nicola Yoon has addressed the issues in Everything Everything, but I'm unable to find any credible sources. If she has, that's great because 90% of authors do not do that.<br /><br />Overall, I liked Everything Everything. I had fun reading it. I liked the characters. I enjoyed the story. But I had a lot of issues with it, some deeper than I can personally convey. I personally prefer The Sun Is Also A Star and I would definitely read more from her in the future, but I just don't think Everything Everything lived up to my expectations.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14048668796147456998" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1300532042" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1300532042" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1300532042?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1300532042" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17283286009006889433"><i>“Just because you can’t experience everything doesn’t mean you shouldn’t experience anything.”</i> <br/><br/>This was a combination of <i>We Were Liars</i> and <i>The Fault In Our Stars</i>. What concerns me is the <i>We Were Liars</i> part. Let me explain.<br/><br/>This is a very dialouge-driven novel. Thoughtful but simple, cute and maybe a little cheesy. There's a whiff of insta-love but that isn't what bothered me. It's the plot.<br/><br/>1. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Madeline is sick. She cannot leave the house. Her mother does everything to keep her alive</span></span>
  <span id="freeText17283286009006889433" style="display:none"><i>“Just because you can’t experience everything doesn’t mean you shouldn’t experience anything.”</i> <br /><br />This was a combination of <i>We Were Liars</i> and <i>The Fault In Our Stars</i>. What concerns me is the <i>We Were Liars</i> part. Let me explain.<br /><br />This is a very dialouge-driven novel. Thoughtful but simple, cute and maybe a little cheesy. There's a whiff of insta-love but that isn't what bothered me. It's the plot.<br /><br />1. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Madeline is sick. She cannot leave the house. Her mother does everything to keep her alive and far away from the world, because the Outside would kill her. Madeline however decides she wants do die so she can live. She leaves the house, runs away with a boy and leaves her mother a suicide note. God that was a bitch move. It made me so angry. Madeline acted like such a brat, and I hated her for it. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />2. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The twist. Turns out Madeline never was sick, her mother needs a therapist, and her whole life was a lie...and I still don't know what to think about it. I didn't like it and I didn't hate it. It just made everything seem so pointless. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />There's one quote that I want to talk about, because it keeps nagging me even two weeks after finishing this:<br /><br /><i>“Maybe growing up means disappointing the people we love.”</i><br /><br />I call that <b>bullshit</b>. Honestly it annoyed me so much. That's a pretty depressing world view. Every teenager should scratch that out of their head. Now imagine you're an adult, you have a child and you're so incredibly proud of it. You watch it grow up, learn things, achieve goals, make decisions. You think your parents are disappointed when they look at you? Nuh-uh, I guess they'll be looking at you thinking "Look at that precious little human we created. Look at how bravely he/she/they just went to the grocery store and bought bread rolls" or something along these lines.<br /><br />I'm sure I'll pick up Nicola Yoon's other works. I enjoyed her writing and her characters, and I hope she'll keep surprising me. Just in a more pleasant way.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/kaispellmeier/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17283286009006889433" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1324606847" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1324606847" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15287695406119401091">I can see how this book might be offensive to some people (if you've read it, you know exactly what I'm talking about), but the author absolutely didn't mean it to be and it is just fiction. Plus, if we want to be mad at someone, we should be mad at a specific character. Just sayin'. <br/><br/>When I first saw this book and read its synopsis, I mentally took a step back. ‘‘Hey, didn’t I read this one already?’’ A big déjà vu moment occurred. I, of course, was thinking of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21393526.Magonia__Magonia___1_' title='Magonia (Magonia, #1) by Maria Dahvana Headley' rel='nofollow noopener'>Magonia</a>, which features a characte</span>
  <span id="freeText15287695406119401091" style="display:none">I can see how this book might be offensive to some people (if you've read it, you know exactly what I'm talking about), but the author absolutely didn't mean it to be and it is just fiction. Plus, if we want to be mad at someone, we should be mad at a specific character. Just sayin'. <br /><br />When I first saw this book and read its synopsis, I mentally took a step back. ‘‘Hey, didn’t I read this one already?’’ A big déjà vu moment occurred. I, of course, was thinking of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21393526.Magonia__Magonia___1_" title="Magonia (Magonia, #1) by Maria Dahvana Headley" rel="nofollow noopener">Magonia</a>, which features a character with a similar disease… <br /><br />Except, in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21393526.Magonia__Magonia___1_" title="Magonia (Magonia, #1) by Maria Dahvana Headley" rel="nofollow noopener">Magonia</a>, the heroine is slowly dying but able to wander outside, whereas Maddy can’t leave her own house. As long as she doesn't and isn't exposed to the outside world, everything inside her functions normally. <br /><br />That being said, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21393526.Magonia__Magonia___1_" title="Magonia (Magonia, #1) by Maria Dahvana Headley" rel="nofollow noopener">Magonia</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18692431.Everything__Everything" title="Everything, Everything by Nicola Yoon" rel="nofollow noopener">Everything, Everything</a> are two completely different novels that are worth the read.<br /><br />In fact, it reads so, so well. I started it thinking I would like to finish it sometime this week, but turns out I read it in less than three hours and I'm a slow reader. (Incidentally, uni is kicking my ass b/c of that.)<br /><br />I'm not gonna go ahead and say that the romance is a never-seen-before one, because let's face it. It's the usual boy-next-door story, but with a twist, seeing that the girl can't leave her house... I SO love that the heroine is Black and the love interest White. Interracial romances happen ALL THE TIME, and yet, they aren't as frequent in books and movies and I'm even going to go as far as to say songs. <br /><br />The writing is mesmerizing. TRY to resist it. And hey, there are cute little pictures. How often do you see those in YA? Try never. <br /><br />I have to watch the movie now... Do not disappoint me...<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4356871258540641167">confession time: i actually saw the film first before i read this, which i rarely do. but in this case, it didnt bother me at all! bookworm blasphemy, i know! :P<br/><br/>even though i already knew the story beforehand, the book still had plenty to offer. i especially loved the little nuances and details of maddys notes - it made the story so much more tangible and easier to accept, because lets be honest. this story is a little unrealistic at times (i guess thats the beauty of fiction). also, its very in</span>
  <span id="freeText4356871258540641167" style="display:none">confession time: i actually saw the film first before i read this, which i rarely do. but in this case, it didnt bother me at all! bookworm blasphemy, i know! :P<br /><br />even though i already knew the story beforehand, the book still had plenty to offer. i especially loved the little nuances and details of maddys notes - it made the story so much more tangible and easier to accept, because lets be honest. this story is a little unrealistic at times (i guess thats the beauty of fiction). also, its very insta-lovey, but i thought the interactions between maddy and olly were cute and adorable enough to make up for it. <br /><br />overall, this kept me entertained and engaged. its short with relaxed writing, so this is the perfect book for someone looking for a quick and unique afternoon read!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4 stars</i></b></span>

    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1998092531?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

      My kid
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1998092531" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13054914712499632422"><b>Buddy read with Mini-me!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1494597767i/22732109._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Ok. So this <i>isn't</i> my kind of book. There is literally <i>nothing</i> about the blurb that would tempt me to read something like this of my own free will. Unless this chick sported some mutant powers, came from another planet, or fought vampires in her spare time? No. <br/>Everything...<i>everything</i>...about this story sounds sappy and gross. <br/><b>Gonna have to give it a HARD pass.</b><br/>And let me go ahead and apologize to all the people who feel marginalized or disgusted at the way this book treate</span>
  <span id="freeText13054914712499632422" style="display:none"><b>Buddy read with Mini-me!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1494597767i/22732109._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ok. So this <i>isn't</i> my kind of book. There is literally <i>nothing</i> about the blurb that would tempt me to read something like this of my own free will. Unless this chick sported some mutant powers, came from another planet, or fought vampires in her spare time? No. <br>Everything...<i>everything</i>...about this story sounds sappy and gross. <br><b>Gonna have to give it a HARD pass.</b><br>And let me go ahead and apologize to all the people who feel marginalized or disgusted at the way this book treated such a serious subject as this girl's <i>illness</i>. &lt;--I get it. Not cool.<br><br>However.<br><i>My</i> <b>Everything</b> is the 12 year old little girl pictured above, and after seeing the trailer to the movie, she asked me to read this with her.<br>I know what you're thinking:<br><i>But Anne, you have 4 kids! How can <b>that</b> one mean everything to you.</i><br>I don't know! I love each one of them with <b>all</b> my heart. There's no science that can explain it, but it's true. Each one is the center of my entire world, each one is my favorite, and each of one of them is the best thing that ever happened to me. <br><i>Why?</i><br><b>Because I said so.</b><br>It's Mom Logic. You don't argue with that shit.<br>Anyway.<br>She's always been my <i>reluctant reader</i>, so it wouldn't have mattered what the hell this was about, there was no way I was turning this opportunity down. <br>So. Here I am, reviewing <b>Everything, Everything</b>.<br><i>sigh</i><br><b>Warning: Spoilers</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496081234ra/22880231.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So this is basically a sugary Nicholas Sparks-lite romance for teens. Minus the horrifying endings that come with most of his books...<br>Which is exactly what I thought it would be, and exactly why my 12 year old <i>loooooooved</i> it. And that's FINE. <br>I mean, the only thing that I really thought was <i>great</i> about the story was the length. I was able to finish it in a day, which was a HUGE bonus because I'd promised her that I would read the damn thing <i>before</i> we saw the movie in the theater. <br><b>Cha-ching!</b> Slid in under the wire, just in time to sit through an hour and a half of teenage kissy face and fade to black sex.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496081234ra/22880232.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The ending is pretty controversial, but until I'd read some of the reviews, I really didn't understand why. Mainly, because I don't read shit like this. Ever. <br>But I suppose it should have been marketed as a 'Mama's Fucking Crazy' story instead of a 'Sick Chick Falls In Love' story. Personally, I liked the fact that she wasn't <i>really</i> ill.<br><b>And here's why:</b><br>I got to lean over to my daughter during the movie and whisper, <i>"See?! THAT'S what a bad mom looks like! I'm not looking so evil for not buying you those (f-ing overpriced!) shoes now, am I?"</i><br>Damn straight.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496081234ra/22880233.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ok. And this was the <b>COOLEST</b> part of the whole experience. After we left the theater, she turned to me and said the four little words I've been dying to hear her say for years:<br><b>The book was better.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496082210ra/22880301.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Anyway, my kid gave it <b>5 OMG-IT-WAS-AMAZING!</b> stars.<br>I'm giving it <b>3 OMG-MY-DAUGHTER-VOLUNTARILY-READ-A-BOOK!</b> stars.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2075759184" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2075759184" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2075759184?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553496673" href="/book/show/33931240-everything-everything">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2075759184" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2833865733288965890"><i>“Everything’s a risk. Not doing anything is a risk. It’s up to you.”</i><br/><br/>I’ve had about <b>36 hours</b> to think about “Everything, Everything” and now that I’m actually beginning to write this review I still don’t know how I feel about the book. <br/><br/>It’s a really good and interesting story and to claim that it didn’t captivate me definitely would be a lie. So why do I have those mixed feelings? And why is it still so hard to sort out my feelings and thoughts? I really don’t know, but maybe this review will hel</span>
  <span id="freeText2833865733288965890" style="display:none"><i>“Everything’s a risk. Not doing anything is a risk. It’s up to you.”</i><br /><br />I’ve had about <b>36 hours</b> to think about “Everything, Everything” and now that I’m actually beginning to write this review I still don’t know how I feel about the book. <br /><br />It’s a really good and interesting story and to claim that it didn’t captivate me definitely would be a lie. So why do I have those mixed feelings? And why is it still so hard to sort out my feelings and thoughts? I really don’t know, but maybe this review will help me to realise what’s been missing. And there certainly was something missing, I just can’t seem to be able to put my finger on it. XD<br /><br />Well, I guess we’ll just have to find out, right? ;-)<br /><br /><b>The plot:</b><br />Madeline Whittier has been ill ever since she’s been born. She has a rare disease that’s called SICD and due to this illness she’s unable to leave her house. Just to get in contact with other people and even other things might easily be the death of her, so that poor girl is actually eighteen and has never seen more than the room she’s living in. Well, and the neighbours that just moved in… Of course their handsome and nice son Oliver has immediately attracted Maddy’s attention and if you think that the shit just hit the fan, well, then you’re actually right! *lol*<br /><br /><i>”I keep picturing myself floating high above the earth. From the edge of space I can see the whole world all at once. My eyes don’t have to stop at a wall or at a door. I can see the beginning and the end of time. I can see infinity from there. <br />For the first time in a long time. I want more than I have.”</i><br /><br />So far, so good! Now that this is settled we can finally move to the character’s section and I bet to write about them will help me to figure everything, literally everything out! (No pun intended, I swear! ;-P)<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Warning: From now on there are going to be many spoilers!!! So yeah if you don’t want to be spoiled you better don’t continue!!! XD</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>The characters:</b><br /><br /><i>”Is it always like that?” I ask, breathless.<br />“No,” he says. “It’s never like that.” I hear the wonder in his voice. <br />And just like that, everything changes.”</i><br /><br /><b>Maddy:</b><br /><br /><i>”Ever since Olly came into my life there’ve been two Maddys: the one who lives through books and doesn’t want to die, and the one who lives and suspects that death will be a small price to pay for it.”</i><br /><br />I liked the way she saw the world and thought about things. I loved that she was a bookworm and didn’t only want to see the world but also wanted to be an active part of it. I could understand her longing for more and I swear knowing about her complicated life I really, really, really felt sorry for her. Which she most certainly would kill me for, because Maddy is such a strong person and actually hates it to be pitied for being ill. After they came back from Hawaii my heart ached for her and to read about her struggle was so painful that I couldn’t decide whether I wanted to hug her or yell at her instead! I know why she banned Olly from her life and it definitely was the sensible thing to do… but well your head and your heart sometimes want different things and I think this is a life lesson Maddy had to learn the hard way. =(<br /><br /><i>”I think of Olly, decontamination-cold and waiting for me. He’s the opposite of all these things. He’s not safe. He’s not familiar. He’s in constant motion. <br />He’s the biggest risk I’ve ever taken.”</i><br /><br /><b>Olly:</b> I loved that boy ever since they moved in. Yes, for me it was insta love as well and to all of you who think this is impossible: No it’s not! You can fall for someone and you can fall hard and even though I know that many people claimed it was too fast I still have to disagree. Call it personal experience, but I definitely know what I’m talking about! ;-) <br />So yeah, back to Olly! I loved his humour and the fact that he could be serious as well. I swear the story about “The Bundt” made me laugh so hard!!!<br /><br /><i>”The thing about my mom’s Bundts is that they are not very good. Terrible. Actually inedible, very nearly indestructible. Between you and me.”</i><br /><br /><i>”I gasp. Did the cake just commit suicide? I crane my neck to see what’s become of it, but it’s too dark out. Just then a spotlight illuminates the cake. Unbelievably, it’s still intact. What is that thing made of?”</i> <br /><br />*LOL* Just *lol*!!!<br /><br />That boy certainly was awesome boyfriend material and the more I got to know him the more I wanted him to be with Maddy! I mean seriously there is no better first boyfriend than a guy who’s funny, cheeky, quick-witted, brave, responsible and caring! Those two were just too cute together and I really wanted their ship to sail!! <br /><br /><i>”In my head I know I’ve been in love before, but it doesn’t feel like it. Being in love with you is better than the first time. It feels like the first time and the last time and the only time all at once.”</i><br /><br /><b>Madeline’s mom</b>:<br /><br /><i>”How could you do this to me? After everything?”<br />I want to say something, I open my mouth to say it, but nothing comes out. <br />My guilt is an ocean for me to drown in.</i><br /><br /> Oh man!!! Don’t even get me started! At the beginning of the book I really liked her relationship with Maddy and I thought that they were a good team, but the more I read, the more I began to dislike her mom! Yes, she wanted to protect her girl but she really could have shown a little more sympathy for her daughter! I mean that poor girl lived her entire life in a bubble and then she falls in love and all her mother does is to fire the only person who was ever really close to her. Looking at it in retrospective the entire incident with Carla definitely made sense and I still can’t believe that I’ve been so blind. Still, what Maddy’s mother did is <u>
  <b>U.N.F.O.R.G.I.V.A.B.L.E</b>
</u>!!! I understand that she seems to have a mental illness, but damn if I’d be Maddy I’d be sooo angry at her!! No, scratch that, I know I wouldn’t be angry, I would be furious!!! How could she? How could she do that to her own daughter??? To her own flesh and blood!!! I can’t!!!! I can’t even put into words how much I loathe her for doing this to poor and innocent Maddy! <br /><br /><i>”I knew it was more than that. I had to protect you. Anything can happen to you out here.” She looks around. “Anything can happen to you out here. In the world.”</i><br /><br />Well and maybe I just found the reason why my feelings for this book seem to be so contradictory. As a mother of a child I know that the love for your little one is unconditional and true. You always try to do what’s best for your child, but in Maddy’s case her mother actually did something completely wrong. Sure, from her POV and in her mind her daughter was ill, but this still doesn’t change anything about the fact that she basically ruined her daughter’s life! With her actions she took away all of Maddy’s choices and in the end she even managed to make her ill. <br /><br /><i>”And it’s the wanting that pulls me back down to earth hard. The wanting scares me. It’s like a weed that spreads slowly, just beneath your notice. Before you know it, it’s pitted your surfaces and darkened your windows.”</i><br /><br />So yes, I think that’s the main reason why the book left a bitter taste in my mouth and resulted in the fact that I don’t know whether I liked it or not. The ending and the repercussions of her mother’s actions made me so angry, but then there was the fact that Maddy and Olly got a second chance at love and this actually made me hopeful and happy again. <br /><br />Do you see how much I’m struggling with this review? *lol*<br /><br />All things considered I still think that “Everything, Everything” was a very good book. Sure it had its weaknesses and flaws, but in the end this didn’t change anything about the fact that it was one hell of a page turner. I constantly found myself wanting to know what would happen next and when it comes down to it, this is actually one of the many things that make a good book, a really good book. Right? XD</span>
  <a data-text-id="2833865733288965890" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1901279305" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1901279305" />
    <a title="Justin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2795921-justin"><img alt="Justin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528849864p2/2795921.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1901279305?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justin" href="/user/show/2795921-justin">Justin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1901279305" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14148515540505949676">Alright, alright... four stars. Fine. I did it. We're good. But let's talk about how much I wanted to hate this stupid book. Oh I don't know, maybe because it borrows from like every popular young adult novel ever written. Funny illustrations, one sentence chapters, hipster chapter titles, nods to classic films and books, unique spins on popular board games, boys who wear black, Tumblr book reviews, mushy romance, wild unchaperoned craziness, the internet, super cheesy descriptions of how beauti</span>
  <span id="freeText14148515540505949676" style="display:none">Alright, alright... four stars. Fine. I did it. We're good. But let's talk about how much I wanted to hate this stupid book. Oh I don't know, maybe because it borrows from like every popular young adult novel ever written. Funny illustrations, one sentence chapters, hipster chapter titles, nods to classic films and books, unique spins on popular board games, boys who wear black, Tumblr book reviews, mushy romance, wild unchaperoned craziness, the internet, super cheesy descriptions of how beautiful someone is, a boy describing himself as sexy, some rare disease that love can overcome, boy and girl falling in love but would never actually in real life so you have to really suspend belief, parents who just don't understand, teenage angst, a bright colorful book cover with giant title font, an author with a cool name, first person narrative...<br /><br />But why... why am I here 24 hours later having finished the book in two sittings and now somehow rating it four stars? God, I have no idea. I didn't even wanna read it. I put it on hold at the library for some stupid reason and when I went to pick it up they couldn't find it. I told them not to even bother because the book probably sucks anyway, and I'd rather read something much better. They insisted and went to check in the back and then came back after taking forever and handed it over. The bright, happy cover pissed me off and I almost threw it back in the librarian's face and told her to forget it. I'm not reading this garbage. <br /><br />It sits around the house for a few days. I finish a couple books, and it sits there beckoning to me from afar. I gave in. I read a few pages and then they just keep turning. I'm thinking about how I've seen all that stuff before. Move along. Nothing new to see here. Pages keep turning. The romance is so over the top and obnoxious. I keep reading. It kinda gets outta control. I keep going. The ending. I really enjoyed it. It's not the most original book in the world, but it far exceeded my expectations on a gray Sunday afternoon. Suspend belief and just go with it. That's what I always say. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14148515540505949676" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText17596224473998663197" style="display:none"><b>Update: 10/29/16 - $1.99 on kindle. Her mother is a doctor and they have a woman named Carla that watches her when her mom is out. She has to take her vitals every few hours. <div id="review_1960985862" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1960985862" />
    <a title="Federico DN" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29005117-federico-dn"><img alt="Federico DN" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478986000p2/29005117.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1960985862?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Federico DN" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Federico DN" href="/user/show/29005117-federico-dn">Federico DN</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29005117-federico-dn?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1960985862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16750614622999876319">It's difficult to live when everything in the world kills you.<br/><br/>In this moderately short but powerful novel we learn the story of Madeline "Maddy" Whittier, a fragile seventeen year old young lady with SCID, also known as the "bubble boy" disease.<br/><br/>Isolated from the outside world, from everything, and everyone, Madeline lives secluded in a completely sterilized house; with a protective mother and a dedicated nurse that constantly checks her medical condition, since even the slightest alteration, eve</span>
  <span id="freeText16750614622999876319" style="display:none">It's difficult to live when everything in the world kills you.<br /><br />In this moderately short but powerful novel we learn the story of Madeline "Maddy" Whittier, a fragile seventeen year old young lady with SCID, also known as the "bubble boy" disease.<br /><br />Isolated from the outside world, from everything, and everyone, Madeline lives secluded in a completely sterilized house; with a protective mother and a dedicated nurse that constantly checks her medical condition, since even the slightest alteration, even the most innocuous microbe, has the potential to kill her.<br /><br />Recluse in a house that she is never allowed to leave, life goes on relatively uneventful, until one day a dysfunctional family moves into the next house. And among them, a young boy named Olly.<br /><br />This external interference, will slowly change her life, unleashing a new world unknown before within her, and a passion to live, that carries, given her fragile condition, a sure risk of death.<br /><br />There are books that make you feel, think, and even tear, and this is one that includes a little bit of everything, with even some laughs as well. It left me with countless quotes and moments to remember. A memorable YA, adorable as few others.<br /><br />**** The movie manages to capture some of the book's spirit, but not really that much. Neither good or bad, just regular. Some important omissions and deviations were noticed. And the atmosphere felt a lot more early teen than young adult. Rue was also there. Interesting to complement the reading. At the very least I'm thankful they didn't butchered the book in the process.<br /><br />Still remaining, The Sun Is Also a Star, someday.<br /><br />Until next time,<br /><br />-----------------------------------------------<br /><br />Es difícil vivir cuando todo en el mundo te mata. <br /><br />En esta moderadamente corta pero poderosa novela conocemos la historia de Madeline "Maddy" Whittier, una frágil jovencita de diecisiete años con SCID, también conocida como la enfermedad del "niño burbuja".<br /><br />Aislada del exterior, de todo y de todos, Madeline vive recluida en una casa completamente esterilizada; junto a una protectora madre y una dedicada enfermera que constantemente revisan su condición médica, ya que la menor alteración, hasta el más inocuo de los microbios, tiene el potencial de matarla. <br /><br />Recluida en una casa de la que jamás puede salir, la vida transcurre relativamente sin sobresaltos, hasta que un día una problemática familia se muda a la casa contigua. Y entre ellos, un jovenzuelo llamado Olly.<br /><br />Esta intromisión del exterior, paulatinamente, irá cambiándole la vida, desatando un nuevo mundo desconocido dentro ella, y una pasión por vivir, que lleva consigo, dada su frágil condición, un seguro riesgo de morir.<br /><br />Hay libros que te hacen sentir, pensar, y hasta lagrimear, y éste es uno que incluye un poco de todo, inclusive hasta alguna risa también. Me llevo innumerables frases y momentos para el recuerdo. Un YA memorable. Adorable como pocos.<br /><br />*** La película llega a capturar algo del espíritu del libro, pero hasta ahí. Ni buena ni mala, veíble. Se notaron varias omisiones críticas, y algunas desviaciones importantes. Y el clima parecía mucho más early teen que young adult. Rue también está ahí. Interesante para complementar la lectura. Al menos se agradece que no masacraran la obra original.<br /><br />Queda pendiente algún día ojear The Sun Is Also a Star.<br /><br />Hasta la próxima,</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1237162816" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1237162816" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30035966-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523817330p2/30035966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1237162816?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/30035966-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1237162816" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2971375533548887537"><i>
  <b>"Maybe we can't predict everything, but we can predict some things. For example, I am certainly going to fall in love with Olly... It's almost certainly going to be a disaster."</b>
</i> <br/><br/>Can we first just talk about this cover??? Amazing right?! Stunning. It fits the story so well.<br/><br/><i>Everything Everything </i>is a novel about a girl named Madeline who is suffering from SCID... or as I knew it "bubble boy syndrome". Madeline has spent the last 18 years trapped inside her house. The only people she comes in c</span>
  <span id="freeText2971375533548887537" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>"Maybe we can't predict everything, but we can predict some things. For example, I am certainly going to fall in love with Olly... It's almost certainly going to be a disaster."</b>
</i> <br><br>Can we first just talk about this cover??? Amazing right?! Stunning. It fits the story so well.<br><br><i>Everything Everything </i>is a novel about a girl named Madeline who is suffering from SCID... or as I knew it "bubble boy syndrome". Madeline has spent the last 18 years trapped inside her house. The only people she comes in contact with are her nurse Carla and her mother. That is until Olly moves in next door. Madeline is a very sweet lead. Also loved how diverse she is. She is a combination of Asian and African American, this set her apart from other YA characters right off the bat and was a huge plus for me. The other thing is her kind heart. I've read characters before who are caring, kind, and sweet but something about how Yoon presents Maddy's traits made it something special. She is a lead that you will easily be able to fall for. She was a lead that I thought I would mainly just sympathy for, but Yoon has this way of just making you more hopefully for her than anything else. <br><br>Then we have Olly the adorable boy next door. He is another character that you will have no trouble liking. I did want a little more out of him, but overall happy with what he gives us. My favorite part of the whole book is with him and his mother bundt cake... So cute I found myself blushing the whole scene. Olly is charming, funny, and I think he seems his age. You might be a little confused about what I just said so I'll sum it up real quick... You know how in other "sick kid books" such a <i>TFIOS </i>a lot of people's issues with Hazel and Gus is that they speak so mature for their age and it's off putting for a few. Some get that it's because they are dealing with a more adult issue of realizing that they are going to die way before their time but some still think they seem a little too mature... So if you didn't like <i>TFIOS </i>for that reason <i>Everything Everything</i> might be more up your alley. Both Olly and Maddy feel, talk, and act more their age. Their relationship can be summed up in one word: Sweet. It's so so sweet. The fact that neither of them is put of by the others life situations is so endearing. You will be cheering for these two and without a doubt you'll want to see them end up together with a happy ever after. <br><br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-wh3XHTkISns/VfWFNjapLAI/AAAAAAAACR0/QrM8OvwufDc/s1600/bubble%2Bboy.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="126" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442155083ra/16198237.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><br><i>Everything Everything's</i> plot is pretty steady through out. But not gonna lie, the plot was actually my "biggest" issue with this novel. The story is predictable. There was never a time when I didn't know what was going to happen next. As soon as Olly is introduced I was like "<i>well... I know exactly where this story is headed". </i>Sure enough I was waiting around for some kind of big surprise twist that I never ended up getting. So why the higher rating? Well because all of the adorable and perfectly placed extras. Yoon gives of these cute little sidenotes, little letters, poems and more. They're just wonderful and wiped away any "errors" I might have felt the plot had. And even with me saying that the book was predictable I really did enough the story. <br><br><b>
  <i>"Spoiler alert: Love is worth everything. Everything." </i>
</b><br><br>I am not a contemporary fan... in fact it is my least favorite genre so liking this book was kind of a big deal for me. <i>Everything Everything </i>is the prefect quick sweet summer read.<br><br><br><b>READ THIS REVIEW AND OTHERS OVER ON OUR BLOG:</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="2971375533548887537" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Just about anything can make her sick and that would be the end for her.<br><a href="http://imgur.com/wzyXaiK" rel="nofollow noopener">

Or even breathe the same air as.<br><a href="http://imgur.com/gcVLRh6" rel="nofollow noopener">

  <span id="freeText80477783138486350" style="display:none"><b>When the ending doesn't matter...</b><br><br>I, like a lot of you, I'm sure, totally called the ending of this thing before I even opened the book - and, for once, I didn't even care. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1510861473ra/24462232.gif" width="268" height="268" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I really enjoyed this story and the characters. <br><br>And I really love Yoon's writing style. <br>The mixed media format was really fun and creative and I had a lot of fun with it. <br><br>I have read a LOT of books in my life - over 1700 - and, I must say, this is the first time I have ever found myself physically spinning a book in circles like a total jackass to read some of the text. <br><br>So that was fun. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476169940ra/20807611.gif" width="500" height="240" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Most of all, I just really liked how Yoon posed some good questions - is life without risk really living? - in such a smooth and lighthearted fashion. <br><br>Anyway, I know this book has probably been reviewed and booktubed to death, so I'l stop there. <br> <br>I have been on quite the high fantasy, YA fantasy, and YA fiction kick lately, so of course I already bought the other book this author recently put out. <br><br>#NoSelfControl<br><br>Prepare to be bombarded with random AF reviews, my friends. <br><br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/SteamyReadsBlog/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
